###begin title 68
The Functions of DNT1 and Spz Are Specific to Neuronal Modality
###end title 68
###begin p 69
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 80 88 80 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 130 134 130 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 147 156 147 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g003">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 162 163 162 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">9</xref>
###xml 316 324 316 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 404 412 404 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 418 419 418 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g007">7</xref>
###xml 513 514 513 514 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 519 521 519 521 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 510 521 510 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz<sup>2</sup> DNT1<sup>41</sup></italic>
###xml 539 542 539 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 544 552 544 552 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
spz is also expressed in bands along the location of embryonic lateral muscles (Figure 9A), in a complementary pattern to that of DNT1 in muscles (Figures 3E and 9B), suggesting that they may aid targeting by different axonal projections. Loss of Spz function affects predominantly targeting by the SNa motor axons (Figure 9C). Loss of DNT1 affects ISNb/d projections more severely that SNa projections (Figure 7M and 7N). The SNa axonal phenotype of double-mutant embryos lacking both DNT1 and Spz functions (spz2 DNT141) is epistatic to spz (Figure 9C). Altogether, these observations suggest that the targeting functions of DNT1 and Spz depend on neuronal modality.
###end p 69

###xml 401 407 401 407 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eo3444</sup>
###xml 411 413 411 413 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 417 418 417 418 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 397 418 397 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2<sup>eo3444</sup>DNT1<sup>41</sup> spz<sup>2</sup></italic>

###xml 603 609 603 609 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eo3444</sup>
###xml 613 615 613 615 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 599 615 599 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2<sup>eo3444</sup>DNT1<sup>41</sup></italic>
###xml 633 639 633 639 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eo3444</sup>
###xml 643 645 643 645 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 649 650 649 650 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 629 650 629 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2<sup>eo3444</sup>DNT1<sup>41</sup> spz<sup>2</sup></italic>
(C and D) Quantifications of axonal phenotypes are colour coded by genotype: controls in blue; single mutants in gold; double mutants in red; and triple mutants in dark brown. (C) Axonal phenotypes of the SNa motor axons, quantification on the right. There is a significantly higher percentage of hemisegments with axonal misrouting defects in the SNa projections in spz2 , spz2DNT141 double, and DNT2eo3444DNT141 spz2 triple mutants than in DNT141 mutants. No significant increase in axonal misroutings was found for ISNb/d projections in spz2 mutants. (D) ISNb/d phenotypes in DNT2 eo3444/Df6092, DNT2eo3444DNT141 double-, and DNT2eo3444DNT141 spz2 triple-mutant embryos. Both the frequency and severity of misrouting phenotypes (arrowheads) increase in the double and triple mutants, including loss of all projections (asterisks). Two hemisegments are shown for the triple mutant.
###end p 73

###begin title 75
###xml 8 18 8 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
A Third Drosophila Neurotrophin, DNT2
###end title 75
###begin p 76
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 18 21 18 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 26 39 26 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5 (CG9972)</italic>
###xml 68 70 68 70 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b045">45</xref>
###xml 77 85 77 85 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-st002">Table S2</xref>
###xml 234 242 234 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">(CG7104)</italic>
###xml 252 260 252 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">(CG9196)</italic>
###xml 306 314 306 314 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-st002">Table S2</xref>
###xml 364 373 364 373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sg005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 210 215 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
DNT1 is closer to spz and spz5 (CG9972) than to the other paralogs [45] (see Table S2). Structure-based alignment using FUGUE reveals that DNT1/Spz2, Spz, and Spz5 are more closely related to each other and to human NTs, whereas Spz3 (CG7104) and Spz6 (CG9196) are less closely related to vertebrates NTs (Table S2). Spz5 is very highly conserved amongst insects (Figure S5B).
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 28 35 28 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GC14928</italic>
###xml 245 249 245 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Spz6</italic>
###xml 254 258 254 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Spz4</italic>
###xml 323 325 323 325 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b045">45</xref>
###xml 516 518 516 518 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b045">45</xref>
###xml 535 538 535 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 584 593 584 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1/spz2</italic>
###xml 595 598 595 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 604 608 604 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 634 638 634 638 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz3</italic>
###xml 640 644 640 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz4</italic>
###xml 650 654 650 654 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz6</italic>
###xml 776 780 776 780 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz3</italic>
###xml 783 784 783 784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</italic>
###xml 791 792 791 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</italic>
The Cysknots of Spz3, Spz4 (GC14928), and Spz6 differ from the canonical NT Cysknot: Spz3 and Spz4 have two extra cysteines and the Spz6 Cysknot lacks two of the conserved cysteines and has three extra ones in unusual locations. The Cysknots of Spz6 and Spz4 also differ from the rest in that they lack a conserved intron [45]. Furthermore, Spz4 is closest to coagulogen (29% identity), while also being closer to Spz3 (51% identity) than to other paralogs, and its expression is up-regulated upon immune challenge [45]. Thus, the six spz paralogs fall into two groups: one formed by DNT1/spz2, spz, and spz5, and the other formed by spz3, spz4, and spz6. Nevertheless, at least five of the six paralogs are expressed in the nervous system. There are no mutants available for spz3, -4, and -6. Structural considerations suggest that Spz5 could also have neurotrophic function.
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 23 27 23 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 98 102 98 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 146 154 146 154 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 170 178 170 178 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 384 388 384 388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 390 400 390 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UASDNT2 CK</italic>
###xml 423 431 423 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ElavGAL4</italic>
###xml 468 476 468 476 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 503 507 503 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 589 595 589 595 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 585 595 585 595 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5<sup>e03444</sup></italic>
###xml 611 625 611 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Df(3L)Exel6092</italic>
###xml 641 645 641 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 694 700 694 700 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 690 700 690 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5<sup>e03444</sup></italic>
###xml 701 715 701 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Df(3L)Exel6092</italic>
###xml 750 758 750 758 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 863 867 863 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 872 876 872 876 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 978 986 978 986 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 1090 1094 1090 1094 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 1096 1102 1096 1102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG9972</italic>
###xml 1107 1111 1107 1111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
To investigate whether spz5 has neurotrophic function we first visualised its expression pattern. spz5 is expressed at the embryonic CNS midline (Figure 8C), in muscles (Figure 9A), in the epidermis (unpublished data), and in the embryonic head peripheral nervous system (PNS) (unpublished data). To ask whether Spz5 can maintain neuronal survival, we expressed the Cysknot domain of spz5 (UASDNT2 CK) in all neurons (with ElavGAL4), which rescues NOCD (at stage 17) (Figure 8D). To ask whether loss of spz5 function affects neuronal survival, we used the only available mutant allele-spz5e03444-and deficiency Df(3L)Exel6092 uncovering the spz5 locus. There is an increase in apoptosis in spz5e03444/Df(3L)Exel6092 transheterozygous mutant embryos (Figure 8D). Altogether, these data mean that Spz5 maintains neuronal survival in the embryonic CNS. Loss of both DNT1 and spz5 in double-mutant embryos results in an increase in apoptosis compared to each of the single mutants (Figure 9D), revealing redundant or complementary functions in the control of neuronal survival. Thus, we rename spz5 (CG9972) as DNT2.
###end p 78
###begin p 79
###xml 33 37 33 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 65 69 65 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 104 107 104 107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 197 203 197 203 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 193 218 193 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2<sup>e03444</sup>/Df(3L)exel6092</italic>
###xml 291 300 291 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1 DNT2</italic>
###xml 366 372 366 372 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 377 379 377 379 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 399 401 399 401 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 362 401 362 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2<sup>e03444</sup> DNT1<sup>41</sup>/Df(3L)Exel6092 DNT1<sup>41</sup></italic>
###xml 404 412 404 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 489 495 489 495 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 500 502 500 502 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 505 506 505 506 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 485 506 485 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2<sup>e03444</sup> DNT1<sup>41</sup>spz<sup>2</sup></italic>
###xml 572 580 572 580 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 735 743 735 743 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 837 845 837 845 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 1092 1100 1080 1088 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g009">Figure 9</xref>
In the muscle, the expression of DNT2 overlaps with that of both DNT1 (in muscles 6, 7, 12, and 13) and spz (in SBM, LT lateral muscles). Both ISNb/d and SNa projections are mildly affected in DNT2e03444/Df(3L)exel6092 mutant embryos. The penetrance of ISNb/d targeting defects increases in DNT1 DNT2 double-mutant embryos, although not significantly (genotype: DNT2e03444 DNT141/Df(3L)Exel6092 DNT141) (Figure 9D). The penetrance of both SNa and ISNb/d targeting defects increases in DNT2e03444 DNT141spz2 triple-mutant embryos, compared to the double or single mutants (Figure 9D). In the triple mutants, misrouting phenotypes can be very dramatic, and there are cases of loss of all ISNb/d motor axons (not seen in single mutants) (Figure 9D, far left). Misrouting of the transverse nerve (TN) can be very dramatic in triple mutants (Figure 9E), although milder effects in this nerve occur with comparable penetrance in all genotypes (approximately10%). Misroutings of ISN are negligible in single and double mutants, but they increase and can be dramatic in triple-mutant embryos (12.7%, Figure 9F). These findings indicate that there is a synergistic interaction between DNT1, Spz, and DNT2 in targeting, suggestive of redundant functions in this context.
###end p 79
###begin p 80
###xml 112 114 112 114 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 108 114 108 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup></italic>
###xml 123 129 123 129 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 119 129 119 129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2<sup>e03444</sup></italic>
###xml 200 202 200 202 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 207 214 207 214 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"> e03444</sup>
###xml 196 214 196 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup> DNT2<sup> e03444</sup></italic>
###xml 231 239 231 239 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-st003">Table S3</xref>
###xml 262 264 262 264 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 269 276 269 276 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"> e03444</sup>
###xml 258 276 258 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup> DNT2<sup> e03444</sup></italic>
###xml 361 363 361 363 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 357 374 357 374 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup> Df(3L)6092</italic>
###xml 399 401 399 401 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 406 413 406 413 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"> e03444</sup>
###xml 395 418 395 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup> DNT2<sup> e03444</sup>/TM6B</italic>
###xml 541 542 535 536 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 538 542 532 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz<sup>2</sup></italic>
###xml 579 581 573 575 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 585 586 579 580 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 575 586 569 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup> spz<sup>2</sup></italic>
Synergism between the DNTs is further revealed by the effects of these mutations in viability. Whereas both DNT141 and DNT2e03444 mutants are viable and fertile, viability is somewhat affected in DNT141 DNT2 e03444 double mutants (Table S3): in homozygosis, DNT141 DNT2 e03444 flies are viable (although some larval lethality, as well as when in trans over DNT141 Df(3L)6092, was observed), but DNT141 DNT2 e03444/TM6B flies do not produce homozygous progeny at 18 degreesC, suggesting unsuccessful larval competition. Whereas homozygous spz2 flies can eclose as adults, the DNT141 spz2 double and triple mutants are completely lethal (100% penetrance). This suggests that DNT1, Spz, and DNT2 play redundant functions for viability.
###end p 80
###begin title 81
Adult Flies Lacking DNT1 and DNT2 or Spz Have Locomotion Deficits
###end title 81
###begin p 82
###xml 54 56 54 56 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b060">60</xref>
###xml 57 59 57 59 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b063">63</xref>
###xml 274 282 274 282 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv001">Video S1</xref>
###xml 289 291 289 291 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 295 301 295 301 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 285 301 285 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup> DNT<sup>e03444</sup></italic>
###xml 310 312 310 312 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 317 323 317 323 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 328 330 328 330 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 306 345 306 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup> DNT2<sup>e03444</sup>/DNT1<sup>41</sup> Df(3L)Exel6092</italic>
###xml 397 405 397 405 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-st004">Table S4</xref>
###xml 465 474 465 474 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv002">Videos S2</xref>
###xml 476 478 476 478 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv003">S3</xref>
###xml 484 486 484 486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv006">S6</xref>
###xml 502 510 502 510 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv003">Video S3</xref>
###xml 515 517 515 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv005">S5</xref>
###xml 534 542 534 542 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv004">Video S4</xref>
###xml 565 573 565 573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv006">Video S6</xref>
###xml 607 615 607 615 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv007">Video S7</xref>
###xml 632 640 632 640 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv008">Video S8</xref>
###xml 646 647 646 647 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 643 647 643 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Spz<sup>2</sup></italic>
###xml 678 686 678 686 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sv009">Video S9</xref>
###xml 20 24 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Neurotrophin mutant mice display abnormal locomotion [60-63].To ask whether DNT mutant flies move normally, we tested the ability of adult flies to climb over the rim of a Petri dish and walk along it-something wild-type flies do without difficulty and without falling off (Video S1). DNT141 DNTe03444 and DNT141 DNT2e03444/DNT141 Df(3L)Exel6092 double-mutant flies display a range of phenotypes (Table S4) including: inability to estimate the location of the rim (Videos S2, S3, and S6), falling off (Video S3 and S5), sluggishness (Video S4), inability to climb (Video S6), slow, uncoordinated movements (Video S7), and wobbling (Video S8); Spz2 mutant flies can barely walk (Video S9). These phenotypes may be due to abnormal targeting or muscle structure or function or synaptic activity. They suggest that an involvement of DNTs in higher neuronal functions is a possibility.
###end p 82
###begin title 83
Discussion
###end title 83
###begin p 84
###xml 116 126 116 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
We provide bioinformatic and functional evidence that DNT1 is a NT, and it forms a family with at least two further Drosophila NT members, Spz and DNT2.
###end p 84
###begin p 85
###xml 45 55 45 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 804 813 804 813 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Amphioxus</italic>
###xml 1334 1337 1334 1337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 1359 1363 1359 1363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 1368 1372 1368 1372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 1408 1412 1408 1412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 753 758 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 804 813 <span type="species:ncbi:7740">Amphioxus</span>
Neurotrophic factors had been anticipated in Drosophila but not previously found. We have identified DNT1 and shown that it satisfies the criteria to be a NT superfamily member. First, DNT1 was identified by sequence homology to NTs through sequence-based bioinformatic searches. Sequence identity to NTs is not high and is restricted to the Cysknot domain. However, this conservation is sufficient to ensure the structural features of a NT Cysknot. Second, DNT1 is structurally a NT superfamily member. DNT1 is predicted to be secreted, it is cleaved and forms a NT-Cysknot, which dimerises to become functional. A structure-based alignment shows conservation of all the residues relevant to forming the Cysknot, not only between DNT1, vertebrate, and human NTs, but also including the ancient NTs from Amphioxus, sea urchin, and acorn worm. Third, DNT1 functions like a canonical NT: loss of DNT1 function results in increased neuronal apoptosis, gain of DNT1 function rescues NOCD, and interfering with DNT1 function affects targeting by embryonic motor axons. In the CNS, neuronal survival depends on DNT1 produced in limiting amounts from the midline intermediate target. Targeting by the motor axons requires DNT1 at the muscle. The high conservation of DNT1 in insects supports its functional relevance. Adult flies mutant for spz or double mutant for DNT1 and DNT2 have distinct locomotion deficits. DNT1 is expressed in the brain, in the centres for learning and memory, suggesting possible higher neuronal functions.
###end p 85
###begin title 86
###xml 15 25 15 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
A NT Family in Drosophila Formed by DNT1, DNT2, and Spz
###end title 86
###begin p 87
###xml 151 153 151 153 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b040">40</xref>
###xml 154 156 154 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b047">47</xref>
###xml 157 159 157 159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b049">49</xref>
###xml 242 244 242 244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b041">41</xref>
###xml 245 247 245 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b043">43</xref>
Previous reports had revealed an NGF domain in Spz and biochemical evidence supports a similar mechanism of activation for Spz and the vertebrate NTs [40,47,49]. A theoretical structural analysis of Spz had shown that Spz forms a NT Cysknot [41,43] . These are features also found in DNT1. However, when we carried out bioinformatic searches for Spz, a relationship between Spz and the NTs could not be established. Sequence identity between Spz and NGF is lower than for DNT1 and BDNF. Spz is also less conserved in insects than DNT1 is. The sequence of Spz is more diverged from the vertebrate NTs than DNT1 is. Nevertheless, Spz, together with Toll, also plays neurotrophic functions.
###end p 87
###begin p 88
###xml 27 30 27 30 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 564 568 564 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz5</italic>
###xml 572 576 572 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 608 618 608 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
Structural analysis of the spz paralogs indicates that DNT1, Spz, and Spz5 are more closely related to each other and to the NTs, whereas Spz3, Spz4, and Spz6 are highly diverged. We cannot at this stage rule out the possibility that Spz3, Spz4, and Spz6 may also play functions in the nervous system. Spz5 is structurally close to the NTs and very highly conserved in insects. We have shown that Spz5/DNT2 has neurotrophic functions, as it rescues NOCD, and loss of Spz5/DNT2 function results in increased CNS apoptosis and axon targeting errors. We have renamed spz5 as DNT2. Thus, there is a NT family in Drosophila formed of at least DNT1/Spz2, DNT2/Spz5, and Spz.
###end p 88
###begin title 89
Neurotrophin Superfamily: High Sequence Divergence in the Invertebrate NTs
###end title 89
###begin p 90
###xml 63 67 63 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 92 96 92 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BDNF</italic>
###xml 116 120 116 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 126 130 126 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BDNF</italic>
###xml 141 145 141 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BDNF</italic>
###xml 203 205 203 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 235 239 235 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 255 257 255 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 285 287 285 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 289 298 289 298 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 316 320 316 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 325 328 325 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Spz</italic>
###xml 357 362 357 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sk-NT</italic>
###xml 413 417 413 417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 426 429 426 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NTs</italic>
###xml 691 695 691 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 697 701 697 701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 707 710 707 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 723 725 723 725 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 806 809 806 809 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NTs</italic>
###xml 928 930 928 930 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 933 935 933 935 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b038">38</xref>
###xml 967 971 967 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 976 979 976 979 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 1002 1004 1002 1004 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1352 1354 1349 1351 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b041">41</xref>
###xml 1434 1443 1431 1440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 1467 1469 1464 1466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1486 1497 1483 1494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Urbilateria</italic>
###xml 1573 1575 1570 1572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1631 1633 1628 1630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1667 1671 1664 1668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BDNF</italic>
###xml 1673 1676 1670 1673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NGF</italic>
###xml 1678 1681 1675 1678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT3</italic>
###xml 1687 1690 1684 1687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT4</italic>
###xml 1782 1786 1779 1783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 1788 1792 1785 1789 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 1798 1801 1795 1798 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
Orthologs are genes related by ancestry. The identification of DNT1 by sequence homology to BDNF does not mean that DNT1 is a BDNF ortholog. BDNF resulted from the duplication of an ancestral vertebrate NT, thus a relationship between DNT1 and vertebrate NTs goes back to an ancestral NT (Figure 10A). Consistently, DNT1 and Spz are more closely related to Sk-NT from acorn worm. The sequence relatedness between DNT1 and the NTs is unlikely to be due to convergence since it was found using three independent types of searches, including a structure-based search, and confirmed with two types of reverse searches, and biochemical features and function are also conserved. Direct proof that DNT1, DNT2, and spz are general NT orthologs cannot be obtained. High sequence divergence amongst all invertebrate NTs precludes the phylogenies to resolve. The same conclusion had been reached for the analysis of ancient deuterostomian NTs [38]. Our phylogenetic analyses of DNT1 and spz compared to all known NTs, revealed interesting features: first, the invertebrate deuterostomian NTs are closer to DNT1 and Spz than the vertebrate NT. Second, amongst those, acorn worm NT (Sk-NT) is the closest to DNT1 and Spz. Third, two other protein families contain Cysknots, TGFbeta and PDGF, but these Cysknots differ from that of NTs. The Cysknot in DNT1 and Spz [41] is unequivocally closer to the NT Cysknot. The most parsimonious explanation (Figure 10A) is that an ancestral NT gene present in Urbilateria (the presumed common ancestor of all bilateral organisms) gave rise to the NTs in deuterostomes and in protostomes. The deuterostome NT duplicated twice to give rise to BDNF, NGF, NT3, and NT4 in vertebrates, and the protostome ancestor duplicated more than once to generate at least DNT1, DNT2, and spz, while sequences diverged, retaining the structural features of the NT Cysknot that enabled function.
###end p 90
###begin title 91
A Common Origin for the NT Superfamily Underlies Nervous System Structure and Function
###end title 91
###begin p 92
###xml 54 64 54 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 98 107 98 107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Amphioxus</italic>
###xml 168 179 168 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Urbilateria</italic>
###xml 219 221 219 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 265 269 265 269 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 271 275 271 275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 281 284 281 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 327 329 327 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 396 399 396 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NGF</italic>
###xml 447 453 447 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT6/7.</italic>
###xml 699 708 699 708 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sg001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 98 107 <span type="species:ncbi:7740">Amphioxus</span>
(A) NT superfamily members identified in protostomes (Drosophila) and deuterostomes (vertebrates, Amphioxus, sea urchin, and acorn worm) imply that NTs were present in Urbilateria, their common ancestor. A protostomian NT gene would have duplicated to give rise to DNT1, DNT2, and spz in insects or perhaps earlier. A chordate NT duplicated twice to give rise to the four vertebrate NTs, and the NGF ortholog duplicated again in fish to result in NT6/7. Identified Trk and p75 receptors are also shown; Trk-like receptors lack some extracellular domains. NT receptors and signalling mechanisms may have diversified through evolution. Annelids, flatworms, nematodes, and tunicates are not shown, see Figure S1.
###end p 92
###begin p 93
###xml 316 326 316 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
(B) Hypothesis that the NTs are required in all centralised nervous systems to link structure and function. NTs are also present at least in acorn worm with a nerve net, a diffuse nervous system, where NT may play a subset of functions, suggesting that NTs could also be present in lower animals (e.g., Cnidarians). Drosophila can be used as a model system for NT-related studies.
###end p 93
###begin p 94
###xml 337 339 337 339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b064">64</xref>
###xml 480 482 480 482 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b034">34</xref>
###xml 483 485 483 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b038">38</xref>
A similar scenario is encountered in the tumour necrosis factor (TNF) superfamily, in which sequence similarity and identity between TNF members is restricted to the TNF homology domain where it is also low (19%-30%), but they are nevertheless considered members of a protein superfamily based on structural and functional conservation [64]. Thus, deuterostomian invertebrate NTs (Bf-NT, Sp-NT, and Sk-NT) belong to the NT superfamily based on sequence similarity in the Cysknot [34,38], and we show that DNT1, DNT2, and Spz belong to the NT superfamily based on sequence, structural, and functional criteria.
###end p 94
###begin title 95
###xml 28 38 28 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
Why Had NTs Been Missing in Drosophila?
###end title 95
###begin p 96
###xml 56 66 56 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 75 77 75 77 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b042">42</xref>
###xml 78 80 78 80 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b065">65</xref>
###xml 81 83 81 83 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b068">68</xref>
###xml 149 151 149 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b040">40</xref>
###xml 152 154 152 154 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b041">41</xref>
###xml 291 293 291 293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b041">41</xref>
###xml 357 359 357 359 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b041">41</xref>
###xml 476 478 476 478 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b044">44</xref>
###xml 545 547 545 547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b043">43</xref>
###xml 780 782 776 778 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b037">37</xref>
###xml 783 785 779 781 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b069">69</xref>
It had long been thought that NTs were missing from the Drosophila genome [42,65-68]. A similarity between Spz and NGF had been previously proposed [40,41] but remained controversial. First, structural considerations had also revealed a similarity between Spz and horseshoe crab coagulogen [41], involved in the blood-clotting cascade. However, this study [41] did not use FUGUE, which was developed later to infer structural relationships between distantly related proteins [44]. A later study confirmed that Spz belongs to the NT superfamily [43]. Our phylogenetic analysis does not resolve coagulogen as sufficiently distinct from DNT1, Spz, or the NTs. The Toll signalling cassette is conserved in horseshoe crab, including a Toll receptor and the downstream target NFkappaB [37,69]. Although it is unknown whether coagulogen may also have NT function in the horseshoe crab CNS, it is an intriguing possibility. We show here that FUGUE analysis comparing DNT1 to all proteins of known structure reveals a closer relationship of DNT1 to vertebrate NTs than to coagulogen.
###end p 96
###begin p 97
###xml 57 67 57 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 122 132 122 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 134 136 134 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b042">42</xref>
###xml 137 139 137 139 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b068">68</xref>
###xml 187 197 187 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 384 386 384 386 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b043">43</xref>
###xml 47 52 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 519 523 <span type="species:ncbi:7962">carp</span>
###xml 667 673 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 760 765 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 835 840 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Second, an initial comparison of the sequenced human and Drosophila genomes with BLAST reported that there were no NTs in Drosophila [42,68]. However, this simple BLAST missed 30% of the Drosophila genes and would have missed any proteins with structural conservation despite sequence divergence. In fact, a recent report has reiterated the relationship of Spz to the NT superfamily [43]. We identified DNT1 using searches optimised for distantly related sequences, PSI-BLAST and FUGUE. In PSI-BLAST sequence searches, carp BDNF reveals sequence relatedness of DNT1 to NTs. Reverse BLAST and PSI-BLAST reveal similarity of DNT1 to BDNF from multiple fish species and humans. Structure-based searches with FUGUE demonstrate that DNT1 is structurally related to human BDNF, NGF, NT3, and NT4. Thus, DNT1 retains the features of all four human NTs. Thus, there is high sequence divergence among the NTs that nevertheless retain the functional Cysknot.
###end p 97
###begin title 98
Similarities and Differences in NT and DNT Functions in the CNS
###end title 98
###begin p 99
###xml 109 110 109 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b001">1</xref>
###xml 222 223 222 223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b004">4</xref>
###xml 224 226 224 226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b070">70</xref>
###xml 428 430 428 430 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b071">71</xref>
###xml 431 433 431 433 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b082">82</xref>
###xml 460 464 460 464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 545 549 545 549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 971 975 971 975 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
The neurotrophic theory originally proposed that NTs promote neuronal survival in a target-dependent manner [1], although NTs can also promote neuronal survival prior to innervation and in autocrine and paracrine manners [4,70]. Important evidence that vertebrate NTs promote neuronal (and glial) survival was the finding that exogenous application of NTs rescues neurons (and glia) from NOCD, both in cell culture and in vivo [71-82]. We find that expressing DNT1 either in all CNS neurons or at the midline can rescue NOCD in vivo. Expressing DNT2 or activated Toll in all CNS neurons also rescues NOCD. These findings indicate that, like in vertebrates, the DNTs can promote cell survival. The prosurvival functions of the DNTs are nonautonomous as the three DNTs are expressed virtually only at the CNS midline, but in the mutants, apoptosis is induced throughout the VNC; DNT1-RNAi targeted to the midline induces apoptosis throughout the VNC, and overexpression of DNT1 only at the midline rescues NOCD throughout the VNC.
###end p 99
###begin p 100
###xml 160 162 160 162 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b060">60</xref>
###xml 163 165 163 165 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b063">63</xref>
###xml 166 168 166 168 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b083">83</xref>
###xml 169 171 169 171 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b090">90</xref>
###xml 182 186 182 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 188 191 188 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 193 197 193 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Toll</italic>
###xml 202 206 202 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 342 345 342 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT</italic>
###xml 464 468 464 468 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 37 42 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Loss of vertebrate NTs in individual mouse NT knockouts or their receptors affect the CNS very weakly, and do not generally cause an increase in CNS apoptosis [60-63,83-90]. Loss of DNT1, spz, Toll, or DNT2 function does not cause massive CNS neuronal death either. Nevertheless, apoptosis increases significantly in the embryonic CNS in all DNT mutants. The dying cells are at least partly HB9 and Eve neurons. We did not find significant apoptosis phenotypes in DNT1 mutants or upon gain of function in the developing retina (unpublished data).
###end p 100
###begin p 101
###xml 51 53 51 53 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b060">60</xref>
###xml 54 56 54 56 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b061">61</xref>
###xml 57 59 57 59 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b063">63</xref>
###xml 60 62 60 62 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b072">72</xref>
###xml 63 65 63 65 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b083">83</xref>
###xml 66 68 66 68 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b086">86</xref>
###xml 189 192 189 192 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 195 198 195 198 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 201 204 201 204 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 185 204 185 204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BDNF<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>NT3<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>NT4<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 212 215 212 215 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 219 222 219 222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 208 222 208 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TrkB<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>TrkC<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 464 467 464 467 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 475 477 475 477 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 471 477 471 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup></italic>
###xml 625 628 625 628 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 633 636 633 636 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 621 636 621 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup> DNT2<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
Vertebrate NTs play partially redundant functions [60,61,63,72,83-86]: some can substitute for one another to rescue apoptosis in mutants, and in multiple knock-out combinations, e.g., BDNF-/-NT3-/-NT4-/- or TrkB-/-TrkC-/-, a 20% reduction in motor neurons and a dramatic increase in brain apoptosis, respectively, were observed compared to single mutants. The DNTs play redundant roles in the embryonic CNS in some, but not all, contexts. Expression of activated spz in DNT141 mutant embryos is not sufficient to fully rescue apoptosis (however, we have not tested the reciprocal experiment), but apoptosis increases in DNT1-/- DNT2-/- double mutants, indicating redundancy between DNT1 and DNT2 for cell survival.
###end p 101
###begin p 102
###xml 240 244 240 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BDNF</italic>
###xml 262 264 262 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b060">60</xref>
###xml 265 267 265 267 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b072">72</xref>
###xml 268 270 268 270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b084">84</xref>
###xml 271 273 271 273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b091">91</xref>
###xml 279 283 279 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 638 641 638 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 646 650 646 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 255 259 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Vertebrate NT function depends on neuronal modality: different neurons require different NTs for survival, and increases in apoptosis in the brain were observed when looking at specific neuronal types (e.g., parvalbumin-positive neurons in BDNF knock-out mice) [60,72,84,91]. In DNT1 mutants, we observe an increase in apoptosis of HB9- and Eve-positive neurons, and loss of Eve neurons. Neuronal modality differences are revealed in the targeting by motor axons (see below). Alterations in DNT1 function affect primarily ISNb/d motor axons, whereas loss of Spz function affects SNa motor axons, correlating with complementary domains of spz and DNT1 expression in different subsets of muscles.
###end p 102
###begin p 103
###xml 62 64 62 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 81 83 81 83 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b060">60</xref>
###xml 84 86 84 86 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b063">63</xref>
###xml 194 203 194 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1 DNT2</italic>
###xml 225 226 225 226 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 222 226 222 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz<sup>2</sup></italic>
###xml 522 523 522 523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b002">2</xref>
###xml 524 525 524 525 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b003">3</xref>
###xml 537 541 537 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 75 79 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 92 103 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">fruit flies</span>
###xml 514 520 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
Locomotion deficits and/or lethality are a further feature of NT knock-out mice [60-63]. In fruit flies, some double-mutant combinations of the DNTs and triple mutants die during embryogenesis. DNT1 DNT2 double-mutant and spz2 mutant viable adult flies have distinct locomotion and/or behavioural deficits. Locomotion defects can reflect proprioception or muscle or synaptic problems. NTs play roles in synaptic plasticity, LTP, and behaviour, and altered NT function causes psychiatric and cognitive disorders in humans [2,3]. At least DNT1 is expressed in the adult central brain in the centres controlling learning and memory. Perhaps the DNTs are involved in higher neuronal functions.
###end p 103
###begin p 104
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 310 318 310 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 474 475 474 475 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b003">3</xref>
###xml 599 601 599 601 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b047">47</xref>
###xml 602 604 602 604 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b048">48</xref>
###xml 758 761 758 761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 805 807 805 807 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b043">43</xref>
###xml 808 810 808 810 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b092">92</xref>
DNT1 produces two types of transcripts: the longer contain the Cysknot domain (cDNA3), and shorter ones (cDNA 1, cDNA2, and cDNA4) comprise only most of the pro-domain. We have shown that expression of the shorter isoform does not rescue apoptosis, rather it (and the full-length protein) may increase it (see Figure 4C). This is reminiscent of the opposite functions of the mature and full-length vertebrate NTs in the control of neuronal survival and death, respectively [3], and of the fact that in transgenic flies, full-length Spz is not functional in immunity, whereas the cleaved Cysknot is [47,48]. We do not know whether the shorter DNT1 isoforms play other roles, but conceivably they may modulate the function of mature DNT1, as the pro-domain of spz can inhibit signalling by the Spz-Cysknot [43,92].
###end p 104
###begin title 105
Similarities and Differences in NT and DNT Functions in the PNS and Motor Neurons
###end title 105
###begin p 106
###xml 94 96 94 96 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b060">60</xref>
###xml 97 99 97 99 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b063">63</xref>
###xml 100 102 100 102 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b083">83</xref>
###xml 103 105 103 105 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b088">88</xref>
###xml 106 108 106 108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b093">93</xref>
###xml 177 187 177 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 203 207 203 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 359 361 359 361 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b076">76</xref>
###xml 362 364 362 364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b078">78</xref>
###xml 445 447 445 447 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b061">61</xref>
###xml 448 450 448 450 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b063">63</xref>
###xml 451 453 451 453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b088">88</xref>
###xml 558 560 558 560 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b085">85</xref>
###xml 561 563 561 563 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b093">93</xref>
###xml 705 707 705 707 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b094">94</xref>
###xml 760 770 760 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 926 928 926 928 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b013">13</xref>
###xml 994 998 994 998 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 1123 1127 1123 1127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 1290 1294 1290 1294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Toll</italic>
###xml 1362 1364 1362 1364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b095">95</xref>
###xml 1445 1449 1445 1449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 1604 1607 1604 1607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT</italic>
###xml 1783 1793 1783 1793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 1795 1797 1795 1797 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b096">96</xref>
###xml 1875 1877 1875 1877 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b097">97</xref>
###xml 1878 1880 1878 1880 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b099">99</xref>
###xml 1928 1931 1928 1931 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b100">100</xref>
###xml 2111 2113 2111 2113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b096">96</xref>
###xml 2114 2117 2114 2117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b101">101</xref>
###xml 2118 2121 2118 2121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b102">102</xref>
###xml 2219 2229 2219 2229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 510 514 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Loss of vertebrate NTs severely affects the PNS, and rather weakly affects the motor neurons [60-63,83-88,93]. Virtually all vertebrate PNS neurons require NTs for survival. In Drosophila, the effect of DNT1 mutations in the embryonic PNS is milder than in the CNS (unpublished data). Exogenous application of NTs can rescue vertebrate motor neuron survival [76-78], but loss of individual vertebrate NTs does not induce motor neuron apoptosis [61-63,88]. Only 20%-30% of motor neurons die in triple knock-out mice lacking multiple NTs or all Trk receptors [85,93]. In fact, the main trophic factor maintaining vertebrate motor neuron survival is GDNF, which does not belong to the NT superfamily (e.g., [94]). Motor neurons are not produced in vast excess in Drosophila, but there is motor neuron apoptosis in normal embryos, as detected with the motor neuron markers HB9 and Eve, although the underlying cause is not known [13]. We observe a significant increase in HB9 neuronal apoptosis in DNT1 mutant embryos compared to wild type (although HB9 also labels interneurons). Loss of Eve motor neurons is also observed in DNT1 mutants, as well as loss of all the FasII-positive ISNb/d axons in triple-mutant embryos. It has previously been reported that RP motor neurons can be missing in Toll mutant embryos, although this could reflect an autocrine function [95]. We have not been able to conclusively determine whether motor neuron death in DNT1 and triple mutants is due to the target-derived function of DNTs in the muscle, or an autocrine/paracrine requirement in the motor neurons. Expression of DNTs at the midline could influence the motor neurons within the CNS. Abundant evidence indicates that motor neurons live and function well in the absence of the muscle target in Drosophila [96]. For instance, upon genetic elimination or surgical ablation of the muscle [97-99] and in the absence of muscle-derived signals [100], motor neurons grow towards the muscle but fail to target or target to ectopic sites. In normal embryos and larvae, the projection patterns of motor neurons is very stereotypic [96,101,102]. Accordingly, it would appear that motor neuron survival may not depend on the target muscle in Drosophila embryos and larvae.
###end p 106
###begin p 107
###xml 62 65 62 65 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b103">103</xref>
###xml 71 81 71 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 150 155 150 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Toll-</italic>
###xml 216 218 216 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b095">95</xref>
###xml 490 494 490 494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 499 502 499 502 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 582 586 582 586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 591 594 591 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 610 614 610 614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
Vertebrate NTs influence muscle innervation by motor neurons [103]. In Drosophila, the existence of a muscle-derived sprout-promoting factor to which Toll-expressing motor neurons would respond had been anticipated [95]. We show that a target-derived function of DNTs in the muscle is required for guidance and targeting by motor axons. Loss of function for all three DNTs, as well as gain of DNT1 function, disrupts axon guidance and targeting by motor axons. The domains of expression of DNT1 and spz in the muscles are complementary, and both overlap that of DNT2. Consistently, DNT1 and spz, together with DNT2, affect targeting by complementary sets of motor axons, and the triple mutants have dramatic defects in all motor neuron projections (see above).
###end p 107
###begin p 108
###xml 76 86 76 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 150 153 150 153 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b104">104</xref>
###xml 154 157 154 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b105">105</xref>
###xml 258 261 258 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b105">105</xref>
###xml 262 265 262 265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b108">108</xref>
The larval neuromuscular junction (NMJ) offers the most amenable synapse in Drosophila. There is abundant evidence of synaptic plasticity at the NMJ [104,105]. However, so far, the identification of the responsible retrograde signals has been rather scarce [105-108]. The identification of the muscle-derived secreted DNTs is promising in this context.
###end p 108
###begin p 109
###xml 94 98 94 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Toll</italic>
###xml 139 143 139 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Toll</italic>
###xml 148 151 148 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 234 236 234 236 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b095">95</xref>
###xml 237 240 237 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b109">109</xref>
###xml 264 268 264 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Toll</italic>
###xml 328 331 328 331 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b110">110</xref>
###xml 374 377 374 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 519 528 519 528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sg006">Figure S6</xref>
###xml 812 815 812 815 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b111">111</xref>
All three DNTs are expressed at the CNS midline and in the muscles. At least the Spz receptor Toll is expressed transiently in the muscle; Toll and spz mutants have muscle defects, and Toll is involved in motor neuron synaptogenesis [95,109], although some of the Toll mutant muscle defects may be due to nonautonomous effects [110]. We have also observed muscle defects in spz mutants and most severely in the triple mutants. However, targeting errors were also observed in the presence of normal muscle patterns (see Figure S6), indicating that targeting and putative muscle functions can be dissociated. We cannot rule out the possibility that DNTs may play roles in midline-derived glia or neurons, including motor neurons, or in the muscles. Interestingly, vertebrate NTs also have functions in the muscle [111].
###end p 109
###begin title 110
Evolution of NT Receptor and Signalling
###end title 110
###begin p 111
###xml 171 173 171 173 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b034">34</xref>
###xml 174 177 174 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b112">112</xref>
###xml 299 302 299 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b113">113</xref>
###xml 369 379 369 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 544 554 544 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 612 614 612 614 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b039">39</xref>
###xml 681 687 681 687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lymnea</italic>
###xml 689 691 689 691 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b036">36</xref>
