###xml 692 694 692 694 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b039">39</xref>
###xml 747 757 747 757 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 930 932 930 932 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b034">34</xref>
###xml 933 936 933 936 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b112">112</xref>
###xml 1020 1027 1020 1027 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aplysia</italic>
###xml 1102 1104 1102 1104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b035">35</xref>
Signalling by DNT1 and DNT2 may not necessarily proceed by binding canonical vertebrate-like Trk and p75 receptors. Ligand and receptor pairs do not necessarily coevolve [34,112]. For instance, Toll-like receptors are highly conserved, but bind very different ligand types in flies and vertebrates [113]. DNT1 and DNT2 may bind yet-unidentified Trk and p75 homologs in Drosophila or other receptors that activate equivalent signalling pathways and result in equivalent cellular, neurotrophic responses. Trk homologs were originally reported in Drosophila and subsequently showed not to belong to the Trk family [39]. However, a Trk homolog has been found in the protostome mollusc Lymnea [36,39], suggesting that either Trks may have been lost in Drosophila or not found. Trk receptors are modular, thus exon shuffling during evolution could have led to the separation of domains into different proteins while retaining function [34,112]. Consistently, an intracellular Trk-like tyrosine kinase domain has been found in Aplysia in a receptor, ApTrk, with an extracellular domain unrelated to the Trks [35]. The converse situation is conceivable.
###end p 111
###begin p 112
###xml 440 450 440 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 452 455 452 455 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b114">114</xref>
###xml 538 541 538 541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b115">115</xref>
###xml 603 615 603 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nematostella</italic>
###xml 623 645 623 645 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Caenorhabditis elegans</named-content>
###xml 1097 1099 1093 1095 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b034">34</xref>
###xml 623 645 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">Caenorhabditis elegans</span>
DNT1 may bind a receptor tyrosine kinase, or a TNFR-like receptor (as p75 is), or resembling Spz, a Toll-like receptor, or, as with vertebrate NTs, DNT1 may be a promiscuous ligand binding multiple receptor types. As with vertebrate NT receptors, binding to one receptor type may result also in interactions with other receptors that alter cellular outcomes depending on context. There is a TNF receptor and multiple Toll-like receptors in Drosophila [114]. Signalling by Toll and mammalian Toll-like receptors underlies innate immunity [115], and it is an ancient pathway present also in the cnidarian Nematostella and in Caenorhabditis elegans. Vertebrate NTs are also involved in immunity. Perhaps Toll signalling is an ancient mechanism underlying the functions of both the nervous and immune systems. Interestingly, the extracellular domain of Toll resembles that of Trk receptors (with the unusual combination of Leu-rich repeats and cysteine repeats), and intracellularly, Toll activates a downstream signalling pathway very similar to that of p75, resulting in the activation of NFkappaB [34]. Our data indicate that the evolutionary trajectory of neurotrophin signalling in arthropods travelled through-although may not be restricted to-Toll. DNTs may also bind other receptor types.
###end p 112
###begin p 113
###xml 62 64 62 64 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b030">30</xref>
###xml 67 77 67 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 224 227 220 223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b115">115</xref>
###xml 295 298 291 294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b115">115</xref>
###xml 329 331 325 327 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b030">30</xref>
###xml 585 588 573 576 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b116">116</xref>
###xml 589 592 577 580 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b117">117</xref>
###xml 756 759 740 743 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b118">118</xref>
Toll, p75 and the TNFR family are more ancient than the Trks [30]. Drosophila Spz/Toll, and vertebrate Toll-related, p75 and TNFR receptors signal through NFkappaB (promoting cell survival) and c-Jun (promoting cell death) [115]. Vertebrate Toll-like-related receptors also activate MAPKinases [115], and p75 also activates AKT [30]. These pathways are compatible with the neurotrophic functions of DNT1, DNT2, and Spz. NFkappaB is also involved in synapse formation, synaptic plasticity, learning, and memory, and alterations in NFkappaB function also lead to psychiatric conditions [116,117]. Inhibition of NFkappaB signalling in crabs (protostome arthropods like flies) leads to deficits in learning and memory, functions traditionally assigned to NTs [118]. Conceivably, also higher functions of DNTs may be controlled by NFkappaB.
###end p 113
###begin p 114
###xml 34 36 34 36 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b033">33</xref>
###xml 37 39 37 39 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b036">36</xref>
###xml 40 42 40 42 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b038">38</xref>
###xml 43 45 43 45 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b041">41</xref>
###xml 46 48 46 48 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b045">45</xref>
Our findings and those of others [33-36,38,41,45] suggest that the evolution of neurotrophin signalling may have resulted in diversification of receptors and/or downstream signalling pathways.
###end p 114
###begin title 115
Ancestral Origin of NTs in Animals
###end title 115
###begin p 116
###xml 46 53 46 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aplysia</italic>
###xml 59 66 59 66 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sd001">Text S1</xref>
###xml 444 451 444 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aplysia</italic>
###xml 460 462 460 462 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b035">35</xref>
###xml 512 518 512 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lymnea</italic>
###xml 613 620 613 620 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aplysia</italic>
###xml 710 713 710 713 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b119">119</xref>
We have not found DNT1 sequences in the snail Aplysia (see Text S1). This could mean that NTs appeared independently in deuterostomes and insects, and their similarity is due to convergence. However, it is equally possible that structure and function were conserved despite high sequence divergence, that the sequences have not been found yet, or that NT were lost from some or many animals. A Trk-like tyrosine kinase domain has been found in Aplysia, ApTrk [35], and a bona fide Trk ortholog in another snail, Lymnea, suggesting that the NT signalling pathway is present in molluscs. Our unsuccessful search in Aplysia is likely due to incomplete genome sequence and expressed sequence tag (EST) collection [119].
###end p 116
###begin p 117
###xml 23 34 23 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Urbilateria</italic>
###xml 36 45 36 45 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 311 320 311 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 326 328 326 328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g010">10</xref>
###xml 381 393 381 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nematostella</italic>
###xml 544 556 544 556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nematostella</italic>
###xml 689 701 685 697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nematostella</italic>
###xml 703 706 699 702 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b120">120</xref>
###xml 751 762 747 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Urbilateria</italic>
###xml 850 862 846 858 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nematostella</italic>
###xml 927 932 923 928 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ciona</italic>
###xml 934 936 930 932 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b038">38</xref>
###xml 1004 1007 1000 1003 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b121">121</xref>
If a NT was present in Urbilateria (Figure 10A), then NTs may be important in the nervous system development and function of all animals with a centralised nervous system or brain. What about simpler animals such as anemones and corals, which do not have a centralised nervous system, but a diffuse, nerve net (Figure 10A and 10B)? To ask this, we searched for NTs in a cnidarian, Nematostella, but we did not find a DNT1 homolog. Sequence divergence and/or incomplete EST database may have also prevented the identification of NT sequences in Nematostella. Orthologs of Toll and downstream targets of Toll, p75, and Trk receptors, such as NFkappaB, MAPKinase, and ERK, are all present in Nematostella [120]. Alternatively, NTs may have originated in Urbilateria and are absent from simpler animals, or perhaps a preexisting NT may have been lost in Nematostella and other cnidarians (just as NTs were lost in the deuterostome Ciona [38]), as extensive gene loss is known to have occurred in cnidarians [121]. Consistently with the view that elaborations of neurotrophin signalling underlie brain complexity, perhaps the diffuse net structure of the cnidarian nervous system does not require neurotrophin signalling, resulting in their loss. However, the acorn worm also has a diffuse, nerve net nervous system, and it has a NT and p75 receptor. This suggests that NTs may also be present in other animals with a nerve net, where they may have a subset of functions (e.g., axon guidance, connectivity, or synaptic functions).
###end p 117
###begin title 118
Conclusion and Implications
###end title 118
###begin p 119
###xml 54 65 54 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Urbilateria</italic>
###xml 146 155 146 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 404 413 404 413 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 763 766 763 766 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b122">122</xref>
###xml 767 770 767 770 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b123">123</xref>
###xml 854 857 854 857 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b124">124</xref>
###xml 937 940 937 940 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b125">125</xref>
Our data suggest that a NT was most likely present in Urbilateria, the common ancestors of all bilateral organisms-protostomes and deuterostomes (Figure 10A)-it duplicated independently in vertebrates and invertebrates, and NTs were retained in organisms with a centralised nervous system and/or brain. NTs may be more ancient and have been either retained or lost in animals with diffuse neuronal nets (Figure 10B). Our findings imply that the control of cell survival and targeting by the NT superfamily is an ancient mechanism of nervous system development. Further functions of the DNTs could also include synaptic and neuronal activity, learning, and memory. Our findings support the notion of a common origin for nervous system centralisation in evolution [122,123]. They suggest that in the course of evolution "elaborations of what went before" [124]-an available molecular mechanism involving the ancestral NTs-and "tinkering" [125] with NT signalling accompanied the diversification of nervous systems and behaviours.
###end p 119
###begin p 120
###xml 68 78 68 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 537 547 537 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 510 515 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
The identification of DNTs bridges a void in neuronal studies using Drosophila as a model for understanding the brain. Conserved molecular mechanisms involving the NT superfamily may underlie aspects of retrograde transport, dendrite formation, axonal remodelling, synaptic plasticity, LTP, and learning and memory also in flies-all functions for which NTs are responsible in vertebrates. This work opens a wide range of opportunities to further the understanding of brain formation and evolution and to model human brain diseases using Drosophila.
###end p 120
###begin title 121
Materials and Methods
###end title 121
###begin p 122
###xml 35 42 35 42 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sd001">Text S1</xref>
Details on methods can be found in Text S1. A summary is given below:
###end p 122
###begin title 123
Bioinformatics: Identification.
###end title 123
###begin p 124
###xml 128 138 128 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 153 168 153 168 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Cyprinus carpio</named-content>
###xml 196 203 196 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG18318</italic>
###xml 260 270 260 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 147 151 <span type="species:ncbi:7962">Carp</span>
###xml 153 168 <span type="species:ncbi:7962">Cyprinus carpio</span>
###xml 424 429 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Full-length and Cystine-knot sequences from 28 known vertebrate NTs were used in PSI-BLAST searches () against release 2 of the Drosophila genome. Carp (Cyprinus carpio) BDNF showed homology with CG18318 both in BLAST and PSI-BLAST searches as the only hit in Drosophila. This hit was verified by reverse-BLAST. When DNT1 is used as a query in structure-based searches using FUGUE, it identifies with over 99% certainty the human neurotrophins, comprising BDNF, NGF, NT3, and NT4 as probable homologs.
###end p 124
###begin title 125
Structural alignment and model of the DNT1 protomer.
###end title 125
###begin p 126
###xml 158 161 158 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b126">126</xref>
###xml 225 227 225 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b044">44</xref>
###xml 293 296 293 296 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b127">127</xref>
To verify the homology of DNT1 to NTs, we carried out structural alignments. The sequences for the NT Cystine-knot domains were aligned against the HOMSTRAD [126] () entry of the nerve growth factor (NGF) family using FUGUE [44]. Using this alignment, a model of DNT1 was built with MODELLER [127].
###end p 126
###begin title 127
Phylogenetic analysis.
###end title 127
###begin p 128
Phylogenetic analysis was attempted using sequences comprised with the Cysknot domain only, as sequences diverge considerably outside the Cysknot. Methods used were Maximum Parsimony, Neighbour Joining, and Maximum Likelihood.
###end p 128
###begin title 129
Identification of DNT1 and Spz insect orthologs.
###end title 129
###begin p 130
###xml 65 70 65 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DmNT1</italic>
###xml 75 80 75 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DmSpz</italic>
The BLAST server at FlyBase () was used to identify orthologs of DmNT1 and DmSpz in other insect species (see also: ).
###end p 130
###begin title 131
DNT1 cleavage prediction.
###end title 131
###begin p 132
Cleavage prediction analysis using the ProP server () reveals two high scores at positions 283 and 294. However, the sequence most likely to match the cleavage site of Spz by Easter is FSLSKKR RE at position 498.
###end p 132
###begin title 133
###xml 42 54 42 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nematostella</italic>
###xml 67 74 67 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aplysia</italic>
Search for DNT1 homologs in the cnidarian Nematostella and mollusc Aplysia
###end title 133
###begin p 134
###xml 69 91 69 91 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Nematostella vectensis</named-content>
###xml 119 131 119 131 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">N. vectensis</named-content>
###xml 136 155 136 155 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Aplysia californica</named-content>
###xml 69 91 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">Nematostella vectensis</span>
###xml 119 131 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">N. vectensis</span>
###xml 136 155 <span type="species:ncbi:6500">Aplysia californica</span>
We searched for sequence homologs of DNT1 in the sequenced genome of Nematostella vectensis and the EST collections of N. vectensis and Aplysia californica.
###end p 134
###begin title 135
Genetics and homologous recombination.
###end title 135
###begin p 136
###xml 105 112 105 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sd001">Text S1</xref>
###xml 229 233 229 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 324 329 324 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">white</italic>
For details of the mutants, alleles, transgenic lines of flies, and GAL4 driver lines of flies used, see Text S1. Null alleles for DNT1 were generated by homologous recombination using the ends-out protocol. The coding region of DNT1, including the ATG and the whole Cysknot domain, was replaced by the coding region of the white gene.
###end p 136
###begin title 137
Isolation of cDNA3, cloning, and transgenesis for gain-of-function and RNAi experiments.
###end title 137
###begin p 138
###xml 4 8 4 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 30 37 30 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG18318</italic>
###xml 57 64 57 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG32244</italic>
###xml 70 77 70 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG32242</italic>
###xml 568 575 568 575 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sd001">Text S1</xref>
The DNT1 locus corresponds to CG18318 from release 2 and CG32244 plus CG32242 from release 3 of the sequenced genome (). Full-length cDNA3 was amplified by PCR from cDNA libraries. DNT1 (cDNA3) was sequenced and presents the following characteristics: MW 100, 315 kDa, PI: 6.17. DNT1 is 886 aa long, with a Signal Peptide (1-30 aa), a pro-domain (31-498 aa), a 102-aa Cysknot domain (499-601 aa), and an extended, disordered 285-aa COOH tail (602-886 aa). For further details on this and on the generation of gain-of-function and RNAi constructs for transgenesis, see Text S1.
###end p 138
###begin title 139
RT-PCR and Southern blots for verification of RNAi and homologous recombinants.
###end title 139
###begin p 140
###xml 115 119 115 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 194 196 194 196 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">41</sup>
###xml 190 196 190 196 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1<sup>41</sup></italic>
RT-PCR was used to verify that targeted RNAi in a heterozgygous mutant background resulted in a down-regulation of DNT1 transcripts encoding the Cysknot. Under the same conditions, the null DNT141 mutants do not produce transcripts, whereas heterozygote embryos produce transcripts in normal levels.
###end p 140
###begin title 141
Cell culture transfections and western blotting.
###end title 141
###begin p 142
Cell culture and western blotting were used to verify cleavage and dimerisation of DNT1.
###end p 142
###begin title 143
In situ hybridisations and immunohistochemistry.
###end title 143
###begin p 144
These methods were carried out following standard protocols, except that for Toll stainings, embryos were fixed for 10 min.
###end p 144
###begin title 145
Microscopy.
###end title 145
###begin p 146
Wide-field microscopy was carried out with Nomarski optics with a Zeiss Axioplan 2 and confocal microscopy with Leica SP2 and Radiance 2000 laser scanning confocal microscopes.
###end p 146
###begin title 147
DeadEasy software for the automatic quantification of apoptotic cells.
###end title 147
###begin p 148
###xml 270 277 270 277 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sd001">Text S1</xref>
We purposely wrote DeadEasy software as an ImageJ plug-in, to quantify automatically cells stained with the apoptotic marker anti-cleaved Caspase-3 (M. G. Forero, J. A. Pennack, A. R. Learte, K. Kato, R. L. Griffiths, and A. Hidalgo, unpublished data). For details, see Text S1.
###end p 148
###begin title 149
Statistical analysis.
###end title 149
###begin p 150
###xml 98 99 98 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 121 128 121 128 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sd001">Text S1</xref>
Statistical analyses of all experiments, with rationale, tests applied, confidence intervals, and p-values, are given in Text S1.
###end p 150

Filming of adult locomotion.
###end title 151
###begin p 152
Filming was carried out with a Motic camera mounted on a Leica MZ8 microscope and using Motic Images Plus 2.0 software.

###begin title 164
High Sequence Divergence among Invertebrate NT Superfamily Members
###end title 164
###begin p 165
###xml 98 102 98 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BDNF</italic>
###xml 104 107 104 107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NGF</italic>
###xml 109 112 109 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT3</italic>
###xml 118 121 118 121 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT4</italic>
###xml 136 138 136 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 154 158 154 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LfNT</italic>
###xml 161 170 161 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Amphioxus</italic>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BfNT</italic>
###xml 191 196 191 196 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SpNT1</italic>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SkNT</italic>
###xml 222 226 222 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 240 249 240 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Anopheles</italic>
###xml 251 256 251 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">AgNT1</italic>
###xml 262 278 262 278 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. pseudoobscura</named-content>
###xml 280 285 280 285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DpNT1</italic>
###xml 296 302 296 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dm Spz</italic>
###xml 437 445 437 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 161 170 <span type="species:ncbi:7740">Amphioxus</span>
###xml 172 176 <span type="species:ncbi:7740">BfNT</span>
###xml 262 278 <span type="species:ncbi:7237">D. pseudoobscura</span>
Phylogenetic trees using the Cysknot from all known NTs, representing the four vertebrate groups (BDNF, NGF, NT3, and NT4), the ancient NTs from lamprey (LfNT), Amphioxus (BfNT), sea urchin (SpNT1), and acorn worm (SkNT), DNT1 orthologs in Anopheles (AgNT1) and D. pseudoobscura (DpNT1) and Spz (Dm Spz). Only the Cysknot was used, because there is considerable sequence divergence outside the Cysknot. The structural alignment shown in Figure 1B was used. The trees were built using three methods: (A, B, and C) Maximum Parsimony; (D) Neighbour Joining; (E) Maximum Likelihood. Numbers indicate percent bootstrap with 1,000 bootstraps in all trees.
###end p 165
###begin p 166
###xml 107 109 107 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 189 191 189 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 208 212 208 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SkNT</italic>
###xml 214 218 214 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SpNT</italic>
###xml 224 229 224 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BfNT.</italic>
###xml 224 228 <span type="species:ncbi:7740">BfNT</span>
(A) This tree is unrooted and shows that sequence similarity is higher within the two clades of vertebrate NTs and insect sequences, and that the insect sequences are closer to the ancient NTs represented by SkNT, SpNT, and BfNT.
###end p 166
###begin p 167
###xml 105 109 102 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fugu</italic>
###xml 293 297 284 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fugu</italic>
###xml 652 660 643 651 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0060284-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 715 716 706 707 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0060284-b001">1</xref>
###xml 744 748 735 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 753 756 744 747 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 797 799 788 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1042 1044 1030 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1046 1050 1034 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SkNT</italic>
###xml 1052 1056 1040 1044 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SpNT</italic>
###xml 1062 1066 1050 1054 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BfNT</italic>
###xml 1101 1105 1089 1093 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SkNT</italic>
###xml 1278 1285 1266 1273 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT SkNT</italic>
###xml 1334 1336 1322 1324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1352 1357 1340 1345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DmNT1</italic>
###xml 1362 1365 1350 1353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 1389 1391 1377 1379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1394 1398 1382 1386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BfNT</italic>
###xml 1400 1404 1388 1392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SpNT</italic>
###xml 1410 1414 1398 1402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SkNT</italic>
###xml 1547 1552 1535 1540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DmNT1</italic>
###xml 1554 1557 1542 1545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 1578 1580 1566 1568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1620 1622 1608 1610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1642 1644 1630 1632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1731 1735 1719 1723 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SkNT</italic>
###xml 1800 1804 1788 1792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SkNT</italic>
###xml 1808 1812 1796 1800 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 1817 1820 1805 1808 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 1847 1849 1835 1837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NT</italic>
###xml 1856 1860 1844 1848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BfNT</italic>
###xml 1864 1868 1852 1856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SpNT</italic>
###xml 1062 1066 <span type="species:ncbi:7740">BfNT</span>
###xml 1394 1398 <span type="species:ncbi:7740">BfNT</span>
###xml 1856 1860 <span type="species:ncbi:7740">BfNT</span>
(B-E) These trees are rooted with the only two available alternative roots: TGFbeta from the pufferfish (Fugu) and coagulogen from the horseshoe crab. TGFbeta belongs to the Cysknot superfamily (which also includes PDGF), but the TGFbeta Cysknot is different in structure form the NT Cysknot. Fugu is an ancient fish, which is more useful than using a more evolved sequence. Coagulogen from horseshoe crab was used because it has a Cysknot resembling Spz, and horseshoe crabs are very primitive. There are no more ancient NT superfamily Cysknot sequences that we could have used to root the trees. The coagulogen sequence was added to the alignment in Figure 1B based on the structure-based alignment in reference [1]. In all the trees, insect DNT1 and spz form a separate clade from deuterostome NTs, which is supported by the high conservation of these genes within insects. (B and C) With Maximum Parsimony, rooting the trees either with TGFbeta or coagulogen reveals closer similarity of insect sequences to the invertebrate deuterostome NTs SkNT, SpNT, and BfNT. The tree in (B) lacks acorn worm SkNT sequence. (D and E) Within this low margin of sequence identity (<30%), coagulogen is not sufficiently different from the NT Cysknot. Interestingly, once again, acorn worm NT SkNT appears to be the most diverged of deuterostome NTs. To conclude, DmNT1 and spz as well as the ancient NTs (BfNT, SpNT, and SkNT) have diverged considerably in sequence, precluding the phylogeny to resolve: (1) The trees do not resolve the relationship between DmNT1, spz, and the vertebrate NTs. (2) The relationships of the ancient NTs to the vertebrate NTs and the insect clades varies with the trees, particularly in the case of acorn worm (SkNT). Structural alignment had also revealed a closer similarity of SkNT to DNT1 and spz as well as the vertebrate NTs than BfNT or SpNT. (3) Although Maximum Likelihood is the best method for distantly related sequences, the low bootstrap values in (E) indicate that sequence divergence is too high to resolve the phylogeny.
###end p 167

(1.27 MBTIF).

###begin title 170
DeadEasy Software for the Automatic Quantification of Apoptosis In Vivo
###end title 170
###begin p 171
(A) Anti-cleaved Caspase-3 (Caspase-3) is a reliable apoptotic marker. Codetection of the apoptotic markers TUNEL (magenta) and Caspase (green) in a single 0.5-mum section of a stained embryonic VNC. Single-channel higher magnification details of one cell are shown on the right.
###end p 171
###begin p 172
###xml 824 831 823 830 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sd001">Text S1</xref>
(B) How DeadEasy software quantifies cells. We wrote DeadEasy as an Image-J plug-in. Whole embryos are stained in vivo with Caspase-3 and the whole thickness of the ventral nerve cord (VNC) is scanned under the confocal microscope, sections are 0.25 mum apart, over 100 sections per VNC. A region of interest (ROI) is drawn over the lateral edges of the VNC to eliminate epidermal apoptosis from the counts. DeadEasy is run as an Image-J plug-in throughout the whole stack. Each individual section is processed to identify objects. Identified cells are labelled throughout the stack, and they are classified in 3-D according to minimum volume and also based on minimum pixel intensity. DeadEasy produces a message with the total number of Caspase-3 cells counted in about 1 min per embryonic VNC (or stack). For details see Text S1.
###end p 172

###xml 519 526 519 526 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0060284-sd001">Text S1</xref>
###xml 188 198 <span type="species:ncbi:7165">A. gambiae</span>

###xml 250 259 <span type="species:ncbi:7091">silk moth</span>

Alignment of the Cysknot domain of (A) spz and (B) DNT2 to their orthologs from insects with sequenced genomes, including 12 Drosophila species, three mosquito species (Anopheles aegypti, A. gambiae, and Culex pipiens), beetle (Tribolium castaneum), silk moth (Bombyx mori), and human body louse (Pediculus humanus corporis). Identical residues are shown in white over red; conservative substitutions in red. There is conservation of spz and DNT2 in insects within the Cysknot, lower for spz. For accession numbers see Text S1.

###begin title 179
###xml 28 32 28 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
Muscles Develop Normally in DNT1 and DNT2 Mutants
###end title 179
###begin p 180
###xml 201 205 201 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT1</italic>
###xml 207 211 207 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2</italic>
###xml 217 220 217 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz</italic>
###xml 304 305 304 305 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 301 305 301 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spz<sup>2</sup></italic>
###xml 314 320 314 320 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e03444</sup>
###xml 310 320 310 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNT2<sup>e03444</sup></italic>
(A) Anti-Myosin stage 17 stained embryos, three different focal planes are shown from top to bottom. Arrows point at muscles shown in each focal plane and which coincide with the expression domains of DNT1, DNT2, and spz. No muscles defects were observed in stage 17 stained embryos. Some stage 13-16 spz2 and DNT2e03444 mutant embryos have abnormal morphology and CNS defects, and the penetrance of these abnormal embryos can increase to 20%-40% in the double- and triple-mutant embryos. These severe phenotypes might be a consequence of earlier developmental defects in dorsoventral patterning, as they can be seen prior to muscle development. To ensure that only zygotic functions are analysed, we focus on stage 17 embryos.
###end p 180
###begin p 181
(B) Targeting defects occur independently of muscle defects: here, three different focal planes are shown to indicate normal muscle patterning with loss of axonal targeting. Arrowheads indicate muscles, arrows axons. There are occasional muscle defects at stage 17, particularly in triple-mutant embryos. Thus, it is possible that DNTs may also play functions in the muscle. Axon guidance and targeting phenotypes can be dissociated from muscle phenotypes.
###end p 181
